Eggeling
  1. Now, when Indra’s energies, or vital powers, departed from him, the gods restored them by means of this very sacrifice. Both cups of milk and cups of Sur─Б-liquor are filled: they thereby restore to him his energies, or vital powers. On the northern fire they offer (from) the cups of milk, and thereby provide him 14 with the bright liquor, with the Soma-drink.

рд╣рд░рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА

[рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рдердореЗ]

Eggeling
  1. He (the Adhvaryu) offers (of the three cups of milk) with (V─Бj. S. XIX, 32), ‘By their devotions the buffalos quicken the sacrifice,’–the buffalos, doubtless, are the officiating priests, and devotion is sacrifice: through the priests he causes the sacrifice to prosper, and through the sacrifice the sacrificer 15;–’the barhis-seated one, supplied with Sur─Б and goodly heroes,’ supplied with Sur─Б, indeed, is this barhis-seated sacrifice, to wit, the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л: by means of the barhis (the sacred grass on the Vedi), and the sacrifice, he causes him to prosper;–’they who bestow Soma,’–they thus bestow the Soma-drink upon him;–‘with the deities in heaven,’–they thus place him with the deities in heaven;–‘may we enjoy ourselves,’–the Soma-juice, indeed, conduces

to joy, and so does the Sur─Б-liquor: both the joy of Soma and the joy of Sur─Б he thus secures;–‘worshipping Indra with good hymns of praise!’–for the hymn of praise is food for the gods, and the sacrifice also is food: by sacrifice, by food, he thus makes him successful. Having sacrificed, they drink (of the milk), and thereby increase what is prosperous with him.

  1. He drinks 16 with (V─Бj. S. XIX, 34), ‘The (Soma) which the A┼Ыvins (brought away) from Namuci, the Asura,’–for the two A┼Ыvins indeed brought away that (Soma juice) from Namuci;–‘and Sarasvat─л distilled for the sake of Indra’s strength,’–for Sarasvat─л indeed distilled it for the sake of Indra’s strength;–’that clear, sweet draught,’–for clear and sweet indeed is that draught, Soma;–‘King Soma I now drink,’–it is thus king Soma that comes to be drunk by him. The cups of Sur─Б-liquor they offer (from) on the southern fire 17, and thereby keep him (the Sacrificer) from evil 18.

рд╣рд░рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА

Eggeling
  1. He (the Pratiprasth─Бtr╠е) offers (libations from the cups of Sur─Б-liquor 19), with (V─Бj. S. XIX, 33), ‘What essence there is of thine, gathered from the plants,’ for this Sur─Б-liquor, indeed, is the essence

of both the waters and the plants: by the essence of both the waters and the plants he thus causes him to prosper;–’the strength of the Soma-juice together with the Sur─Б-liquor,’–he thereby secures what strength there is in the Soma-juice and in the Sur─Б-liquor;–‘by that exhilarating drink quicken thou the Sacrificer,’–that is, ‘by that exhilarating drink gladden thou the Sacrificer;’–‘Sarasvat─л, the A┼Ыvins, Indra, and Agni,’–by deities he (the priest) thus causes the sacrifice to prosper, and by deities and sacrifice the Sacrificer. Having made the offering, they drink (the liquor), and thereby cause to prosper what is unprosperous with him.

Eggeling
  1. He drinks, with (V─Бj. S. XIX, 35), ‘Whatever is mingled herewith of the juicy Soma,’–he thereby secures for him the essence (juice) of the effused (extracted) and the infused 20 (Soma);–‘which Indra drank with eagerness,’–for Indra, indeed, drank it with eagerness;–’that (essence) thereof (I drink) with propitious mind,’–for unpropitious, as it were, to a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa is that drink, the Sur─Б-liquor: having thus made it propitious, he takes it to himself;–‘King Soma I drink,’–it is thus king Soma that comes to be drunk by him.

Eggeling
  1. ‘To the Svadh─Б-loving Fathers be Svadh─Б, adoration!’ he thereby places the Fathers with the Svadh─Б in the world of the Fathers.–‘To the Svadh─Б-loving grandfathers he Svadh─Б, adoration!’ he thereby places the grandfathers with the Svadh─Б in the world of the grandfathers.–‘To the Svadh─Б-loving great-grandfathers be Svadh─Б, adoration!’ he thereby places the great-grandfathers with the Svadh─Б in the world of the great-grandfathers.

Eggeling
  1. Here, now, they ask, ‘Is the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л to be performed, or is it not to be performed, seeing that (in any case) they continuously repel from him all evil?’ As to this Revottaras Sthapati P─Бс╣нava K─Бkra once said, ‘Even after making the surrender, one ought certainly to perform the sacrifice; for the Sacrificer is the body of the sacrifice, and the officiating priests are its limbs; and wherever the body is pure there the limbs also are pure; both of them, indeed, purify him, and both of them repel the evil from him: therefore even after making the surrender (of one’s own self) one ought certainly to sacrifice.’

Eggeling
  1. He (the Sacrificer) offers, with (V─Бj. S. XIX, 45), ‘The Fathers who, one in form and one in mind, live in Yama’s realm,–may their world,

the Svadh─Б, adoration, and sacrifice prosper among the gods!’ he thereby commits the Fathers to Yama, and he also conquers the world of the Fathers. Having, all of them, invested themselves sacrificially 29, they betake themselves to the northern fire, for the northern fire 30 is this (terrestrial) world 31: they thus establish themselves in this world. He offers an oblation of ghee: ghee being sacrifice, it is from out of the sacrifice that they establish themselves in the sacrifice.

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдореН

Eggeling
  1. He (the Sacrificer) offers, with (V─Бj. S. XIX, 46), ‘Mine own (people) who are one in form and one in mind, living among the living,–may their fortune prosper with me, in this world, for a hundred years!’ he thereby secures the good fortune of his own people, and he also confers long life on them. Whilst they hold on to each other, he (the Adhvaryu) offers milk, for milk is vital air and food: in the vital air, in food, they thus finally establish themselves.

  1. He offers, with (V─Бj. S. XIX, 47), ‘Two paths for mortals have I heard of, (that of the Fathers and that of the gods 32),’–’two paths

indeed there are,’ they say, ’those of the gods and of the Fathers,’–’thereon all that liveth here passeth,’ for thereon, indeed, everything living here passes;–‘what there is between the father and the mother,’–the father, doubtless, is yonder (sky), and the mother is this (earth): by means of these two he leads the Fathers to the world of heaven. He (the Sacrificer) alone drinks what is left from the offering 33: to himself alone he thus takes prosperity, for milk is prosperity.

рд╣рд░рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрдорджрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╣рд░рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирдГ рдХреГрддреМ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рдиреАрдпрд╢рддрдкрдердмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рдХрд╛рдгреНрдбреЗ рдЕрд╖реНрдЯрдореЗ рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рее (резреи ред рео ред рез) рее

Eggeling
  1. He drinks it, with (V─Бj. S. XIX, 48), ‘May this oblation be productive for me,’–for productive indeed it is, whether it be milk or Soma;–‘possessed of ten heroes,’–the ten heroes, doubtless, are the vital airs: vital airs he thus takes to himself;–‘possessed of all the troops,’–all the troops, doubtless, are the limbs: it is limbs he thus takes to himself;–‘for well-being: breath-winning,’–the breath of life he thus wins;–‘race-winning,’–a race (offspring) he thus wins;–‘cattle-winning,’–cattle he thus wins;–‘place-winning’–for it is for a place (in heaven) that he sacrifices: it is that he gains;–‘safety-winning,’–the (place of) safety, doubtless, is the heavenly world: in the heavenly world he thus finally establishes himself;–‘May Agni raise for me abundant offspring,

and bestow ye upon us food, milk, and seed!’ it is to those (priests) who offer for him that he thus says, ‘Bestow ye all this upon me!’ By means of gold they cleanse themselves 34; for gold is immortal life: in immortal life they thus finally establish themselves.

  1. рд╕реБрд░рд╛рд╡рдиреНрддрдорд┐рддрд┐ рдЬреБрд╣реЛрддрд┐ ред (рдХрд╛. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рд╕реВ. резреп ред ремрек) рддреНрд░реАрдирдкрд┐ рдкрдпреЛрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рдиреН рд╕рд╣реИрд╡рд╛рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрдГ рее ↩︎

  14. 231:1 Or, cause him to prosper, render him successful by means of the liquor; MS. I. O. 311 reads ‘samardhayanti.’ ↩︎

  15. 231:2 Or, perhaps, he provides the sacrifice with priests, and the Sacrificer with sacrifice. For obvious reasons the first two p─Бdas of the verse have been transposed in the translation. ↩︎

  16. 232:1 For particulars as to the persons who partake of the respective cups of milk and Sur─Б-liquor, see XII, 8, 2, 22 seqq. ↩︎

  17. 232:2 That is, on the fire of the southern of the two special Vedis, see p. 225, note. ↩︎

  18. 232:3 Viz. inasmuch as the libations of liquor are not made on the offering-fire proper, the (northern) ─Аhavan─лya, where the oblations from the cups of milk are made. ↩︎

  19. 232:4 These cups are of the same kind as those used for the draughts of Soma, being made of pal─Б┼Ыa-wood, and resembling mortars in shape; cf. part ii, p. 259, note 1, towards the end. ↩︎

  20. 233:1 For the distinction between ‘suta’ and ‘─Бsuta’ (not ‘asuta’), cf. XII, 8, 2, 12. ↩︎

  21. 233:2 According to K─Бty. ┼Ъr. XIX, 3, 15, some authorities, however, think the inhaling of the fumes of the liquor to be sufficient for this purpose. ↩︎

  22. 234:1 The coals are to be placed on the south side of the southern fire, from north to south, and the libation from the ─А┼Ыvina cup is made on the northernmost coal, that from the S─Бrasvata cup on the central one, and that from the Aindra cup on the southern one. According to K─Бty. XIX, 3, 17, and Mah─лdhara on V─Бj. S. XIX, 36, this is a fourth alternative of disposing of the liquor (in favour of the Fathers), the others being actual drinking, or smelling it, or hiring some one to drink it. ↩︎

  23. 234:2 At XII, 7, 2, 13 a perforated pot (with a hundred holes) was mentioned as being used at this sacrifice. According to K─Бty. ┼Ъr. XIX, 3, 20, and Mah─лdhara on V─Бj. S. XIX, 37, use is made of this pot at this juncture in much the same way as is described in V, 5, 4, 27 seqq.; viz. two poles are driven into the ground north and south of the southern fire, and a bamboo stick laid thereon: on a string fastened to this stick the pot, containing a tail-whisk (for straining) and a piece of gold, is then made to hang over the fire, and the remains of the Sur─Б-liquor poured into it; and whilst it trickles through into the fire, the priest makes the Sacrificer pronounce the verses V─Бj. S. XIX, 37-44, 52-60, addressed to the different kinds of departed ancestors. ↩︎

  24. 235:1 That is, verses recited at the Soma-sacrifice whilst the Soma-juice is clarifying; the term being usually confined to the verses of hymns of the ninth maс╣Зс╕Нala of the R╠еksaс╣Бhit─Б, whence indeed most of the verses used on this occasion (V─Бj. S. XIX, 37-44) are taken. ↩︎

  32. 237:4 Not only is the second p─Бda of the verse omitted here (as also in MS. I. O. 311), but the construction of the first half of the verse is also rather peculiar, the most natural rendering being, ‘Two paths of the Fathers have I heard of, (those) of the gods and of men.’ The same verse occurs R╠еks. X, 88, 15 (with the reading ‘dve srut─л’ instead of ‘dve sr╠еt─л’), where Grassmann translates,– ‘Two paths there are, so the Fathers have told me, passable for gods and men;’ whilst Ludwig takes it in the way just referred to. The above interpretation is that of Mah─лdhara, who refers to ┼Ъat.-Br. I, 9, 2, 3; whilst S─Бyaс╣Зa (on Riks.) seems to take the two paths to be that of the Fathers and gods, and that of men (pitr─лс╣З─Бс╣Б dev─Бn─Бс╣Б cot─Бpi marty─Бn─Бс╣Б ca dve srut─л dvau m─Бrgau); though he afterwards calls them ‘devay─Бna’ and ‘pitr╠еy─Бс╣Зa.’ ↩︎

  33. 238:1 That is to say, the milk which remains in the pot (ukh─Б), from which the milk used for the oblation was taken. ↩︎

  34. 239:1 K─Бty. ┼Ъr. XIX, 3, 27, ‘Over the c─Бtv─Бla (pit) they cleanse themselves, with their wives, putting gold between;’ that is to say, whilst the water is poured on their hands a piece of gold is held between, over which the water flows. ↩︎
